**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy Filter Chain Configuration Propagation

## Your Task

Trace how an Envoy HTTP filter configuration defined in a Protobuf `.proto` file in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` gets consumed by the C++ filter implementation in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find: 1. The `.proto` file in `data-plane-api` that defines the `HttpConnectionManager` filter chain configuration. 2. The C++ source files in `envoy` under `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/` that parse and apply this configuration. Report the repo, file path, and key type/class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

```json
{

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Summary

I've identified how Envoy HTTP filter chain configuration flows from Protobuf definition to C++ implementation:

### Key Files Found:

**Data-plane-api (Configuration Definition):**
- `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto`
  - `HttpConnectionManager` message with `repeated HttpFilter http_filters = 5;` field
  - `HttpFilter` message defining individual filter configs with name and typed_config

**Envoy (C++ Implementation):**
1. `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h` - `HttpConnectionManagerFilterConfigFactory` and `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` classes
2. `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.cc` - Config parsing using `FilterChainHelper` (lines 709-714)
3. `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h` - `FilterChainHelper` template that processes each filter by:
   - Iterating through HttpFilter protos via `processFilters()`
   - Instantiating filter factories via `processFilter()`
4. `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` - `ConnectionManagerImpl` executes the filter chain

### Configuration Flow:
1. Proto defines HttpFilter list → 2. Factory parses config → 3. FilterChainHelper instantiates each filter → 4. ConnectionManagerImpl applies filters to requests

The answer file includes files, symbols, call chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the complete flow.

  "content": "{\"content\":\"600:   // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the entire request to be received.\\n601:   // The timer is activated when the request is initiated, and is disarmed when the last byte of the\\n602:   // request is sent upstream (i.e. all decoding filters have processed the request), OR when the\\n603:   // response is initiated. If not specified or set to 0, this timeout is disabled.\\n604:   google.protobuf.Duration request_timeout = 28\\n605:       [(udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true];\\n606: \\n607:   // The amount of time that Envoy will wait for the request headers to be received. The timer is\\n608:   // activated when the first byte of the headers is received, and is disarmed when the last byte of\\n609:   // the headers has been received. If not specified or set to 0, this timeout is disabled.\\n610:   google.protobuf.Duration request_headers_timeout = 41 [\\n611:     (validate.rules).duration = {gte {}},\\n612:     (udpa.annotations.security).configure_for_untrusted_downstream = true\\n613:   ];\\n614: \\n615:   // The time that Envoy will wait between sending an HTTP/2 \u201cshutdown\\n616:   // notification\u201d (GOAWAY frame with max stream ID) and a final GOAWAY frame.\\n617:   // This is used so that Envoy provides a grace period for new streams that\\n618:   // race with the final GOAWAY frame. During this grace period, Envoy will\\n619:   // continue to accept new streams. After the grace period, a final GOAWAY\\n620:   // frame is sent and Envoy will start refusing new streams. Draining occurs\\n621:   // either when a connection hits the idle timeout, when :ref:`max_connection_duration\\n622:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HttpProtocolOptions.max_connection_duration>`\\n623:   // is reached, or during general server draining. The default grace period is\\n624:   // 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if this option is not specified.\\n625:   google.protobuf.Duration drain_timeout = 12;\\n626: \\n627:   // The delayed close timeout is for downstream connections managed by the HTTP connection manager.\\n628:   // It is defined as a grace period after connection close processing has been locally initiated\\n629:   // during which Envoy will wait for the peer to close (i.e., a TCP FIN/RST is received by Envoy\\n630:   // from the downstream connection) prior to Envoy closing the socket associated with that\\n631:   // connection.\\n632:   //\\n633:   // .. note::\\n634:   //\\n635:   //   This timeout is enforced even when the socket associated with the downstream connection is pending a flush of\\n636:   //   the write buffer. However, any progress made writing data to the socket will restart the timer associated with\\n637:   //   this timeout. This means that the total grace period for a socket in this state will be\\n638:   //   <total_time_waiting_for_write_buffer_flushes>+<delayed_close_timeout>.\\n639:   //\\n640:   // Delaying Envoy's connection close and giving the peer the opportunity to initiate the close\\n641:   // sequence mitigates a race condition that exists when downstream clients do not drain/process\\n642:   // data in a connection's receive buffer after a remote close has been detected via a socket\\n643:   // ``write()``. This race leads to such clients failing to process the response code sent by Envoy,\\n644:   // which could result in erroneous downstream processing.\\n645:   //\\n646:   // If the timeout triggers, Envoy will close the connection's socket.\\n647:   //\\n648:   // The default timeout is 1000 ms if this option is not specified.\\n649:   //\\n650:   // .. note::\\n651:   //    To be useful in avoiding the race condition described above, this timeout must be set\\n652:   //    to *at least* <max round trip time expected between clients and Envoy>+<100ms to account for\\n653:   //    a reasonable \\\"worst\\\" case processing time for a full iteration of Envoy's event loop>.\\n654:   //\\n655:   // .. warning::\\n656:   //    A value of ``0`` will completely disable delayed close processing. When disabled, the downstream\\n657:   //    connection's socket will be closed immediately after the write flush is completed or will\\n658:   //    never close if the write flush does not complete.\\n659:   //\\n660:   google.protobuf.Duration delayed_close_timeout = 26;\\n661: \\n662:   // Configuration for :ref:`HTTP access logs <arch_overview_access_logs>`\\n663:   // emitted by the connection manager.\\n664:   repeated config.accesslog.v3.AccessLog access_log = 13;\\n665: \\n666:   // The interval to flush the above access logs.\\n667:   //\\n668:   // .. attention::\\n669:
